Find all implementations and usages of Terraform's `provider.Provider` interface across two repositories.

## Background

Terraform providers are plugins that implement the `providers.Interface` (commonly referred to as `provider.Provider`) defined in the Terraform core codebase. This interface defines the contract between Terraform's execution engine and provider plugins, specifying methods for schema retrieval, configuration, resource lifecycle operations (plan/apply/read/delete), and state management.

The interface is defined in `hashicorp/terraform` at `internal/providers/provider.go` and includes key methods like:
- `GetProviderSchema()` - returns provider, resource, and data source schemas
- `ConfigureProvider()` - configures the provider with settings
- `PlanResourceChange()` / `ApplyResourceChange()` - resource lifecycle operations
- `ReadResource()` - refreshes resource state
- `ValidateResourceConfig()` / `ValidateDataResourceConfig()` - configuration validation

Provider plugins (like terraform-provider-aws) implement this interface, while Terraform core invokes these methods during plan, apply, refresh, and validate operations.

## Repositories

Two repositories are available under `/workspace/`:

- `/workspace/terraform/` — hashicorp/terraform (Go, core Terraform engine with interface definition and internal callers)
- `/workspace/terraform-provider-aws/` — hashicorp/terraform-provider-aws (Go, AWS provider implementation)

## Task

Find **all** places where the `providers.Interface` (provider.Provider) is:
1. **Implemented** as a struct/type (e.g., `MockProvider`, `GRPCProvider`, or provider factory functions)
2. **Called/invoked** as a method receiver (e.g., `provider.ConfigureProvider()`, `provider.ReadResource()`)
3. **Used as a type** in function signatures or variable declarations where the interface methods are actually invoked

Include production code and test code. Focus on concrete implementations and actual method invocations, not just type declarations or comments.

For each implementation or usage, record:
- `repo`: either `hashicorp/terraform` or `hashicorp/terraform-provider-aws`
- `file`: path relative to the repository root (e.g., `terraform/provider_mock.go`, `internal/provider/provider.go`)
- `function`: the enclosing function or method name, OR the struct/type name if it's an implementation (e.g., `MockProvider`, `managedResourceExecute`, `ProtoV5ProviderServerFactory`)

## Output

Write your results to `/workspace/callers.json` as a JSON array:

```json
[
  {
    "repo": "hashicorp/terraform",
    "file": "terraform/provider_mock.go",
    "function": "MockProvider"
  },
  {
    "repo": "hashicorp/terraform",
    "file": "terraform/node_resource_apply_instance.go",
    "function": "managedResourceExecute"
  },
  {
    "repo": "hashicorp/terraform-provider-aws",
    "file": "internal/provider/provider.go",
    "function": "ProtoV5ProviderServerFactory"
  }
]
```

Do not include:
- The interface definition itself (`internal/providers/provider.go` where `Interface` is declared)
- Pure documentation references (`.md` files)
- Type alias declarations that don't invoke or implement the interface methods
- Auto-generated code or vendor directories

### Implementations (Provider Types)

3. **mockProvider** (`internal/refactoring/mock_provider.go`) - Limited mock for refactoring operations

7. **unknownProvider** - Stub provider for deferred operations

11. **GRPCProvider** (`internal/plugin/grpc_provider.go`) - Wraps plugin gRPC protocol
12. **unconfigurableProvider** - Stub for unconfigurable states

p.beginWrite()()\n580: \n581: \tp.ReadResourceCalled = true\n582: \tp.ReadResourceRequest = r\n583: \n584: \tif !p.ConfigureProviderCalled {\n585: \t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"Configure not called before ReadResource %q\", r.TypeName))\n586: \t\treturn resp\n587: \t}\n588: \n589: \tif p.ReadResourceFn != nil {\n590: \t\treturn p.ReadResourceFn(r)\n591: \t}\n592: \n593: \tif p.ReadResourceResponse != nil {\n594: \t\tresp = *p.ReadResourceResponse\n595: \n596: \t\t// Make sure the NewState conforms to the schema.\n597: \t\t// This isn't always the case for the existing tests.\n598: \t\tschema, ok := p.getProviderSchema().ResourceTypes[r.TypeName]\n599: \t\tif !ok {\n600: \t\t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"no schema found for %q\", r.TypeName))\n601: \t\t\treturn resp\n602: \t\t}\n603: \n604: \t\tnewState, err := schema.Body.CoerceValue(resp.NewState)\n605: \t\tif err != nil {\n606: \t\t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.Append(err)\n607: \t\t}\n608: \t\tresp.NewState = newState\n609: \t\tif resp.Identity.IsNull() {\n610: \t\t\tresp.Identity = r.CurrentIdentity\n611: \t\t}\n612: \n613: \t\treturn resp\n614: \t}\n615: \n616: \t// otherwise just return the same state we received without the write-only attributes\n617: \t// since there are old tests without a schema we default to the prior state\n618: \tif schema, ok := p.getProviderSchema().ResourceTypes[r.TypeName]; ok {\n619: \n620: \t\tnewVal, err := cty.Transform(r.PriorState, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n621: \t\t\t// We're only concerned with known null values, which can be computed\n622: \t\t\t// by the provider.\n623: \t\t\tif !v.IsKnown() {\n624: \t\t\t\treturn v, nil\n625: \t\t\t}\n626: \n627: \t\t\tattrSchema := schema.Body.AttributeByPath(path)\n628: \t\t\tif attrSchema == nil {\n629: \t\t\t\t// this is an intermediate path which does not represent an attribute\n630: \t\t\t\treturn v, nil\n631: \t\t\t}\n632: \n633: \t\t\t// Write-only attributes always return null\n634: \t\t\tif attrSchema.WriteOnly {\n635: \t\t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n636: \t\t\t}\n637: \n638: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n639: \t\t})\n640: \t\tif err != nil {\n641: \t\t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.Append(err)\n642: \t\t}\n643: \t\tresp.NewState = newVal\n644: \t} else {\n645: \t\tresp.NewState = r.PriorState\n646: \t}\n647: \n648: \tresp.Identity = r.CurrentIdentity\n649: \tresp.Private = r.Private\n650: \treturn resp\n651: }\n652: \n653: func (p *MockProvider) PlanResourceChange(r providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest) (resp providers.PlanResourceChangeResponse) {\n654: \tdefer p.beginWrite()()\n655: \n656: \tif !p.ConfigureProviderCalled {\n657: \t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"Configure not called before PlanResourceChange %q\", r.TypeName))\n658: \t\treturn resp\n659: \t}\n660: \n661: \tp.PlanResourceChangeCalled = true\n662: \tp.PlanResourceChangeRequest = r\n663: \n664: \tif p.PlanResourceChangeFn != nil {\n665: \t\treturn p.PlanResourceChangeFn(r)\n666: \t}\n667: \n668: \tif p.PlanResourceChangeResponse != nil {\n669: \t\treturn *p.PlanResourceChangeResponse\n670: \t}\n671: \n672: \t// this is a destroy plan,\n673: \tif r.ProposedNewState.IsNull() {\n674: \t\tresp.PlannedState = r.ProposedNewState\n675: \t\tresp.PlannedPrivate = r.PriorPrivate\n676: \t\treturn resp\n677: \t}\n678: \n679: \tschema, ok := p.getProviderSchema().ResourceTypes[r.TypeName]\n680: \tif !ok {\n681: \t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"no schema found for %q\", r.TypeName))\n682: \t\treturn resp\n683: \t}\n684: \n685: \t// The default plan behavior is to accept the proposed value, and mark all\n686: \t// nil computed attributes as unknown.\n687: \tval, err := cty.Transform(r.ProposedNewState, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n688: \t\t// We're only concerned with known null values, which can be computed\n689: \t\t// by the provider.\n690: \t\tif !v.IsKnown() {\n691: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n692: \t\t}\n693: \n694: \t\tattrSchema := schema.Body.AttributeByPath(path)\n695: \t\tif attrSchema == nil {\n696: \t\t\t// this is an intermediate path which does not represent an attribute\n697: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n698: \t\t}\n699: \n700: \t\t// Write-only attributes always return null\n701: \t\tif attrSchema.WriteOnly {\n702: \t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n703: \t\t}\n704: \n705: \t\t// get the current configuration value, to detect when a\n706: \t\t// computed+optional attributes has become unset\n707: \t\tconfigVal, err := path.Apply(r.Config)\n708: \t\tif err != nil {\n709: \t\t\t// cty can't currently apply some paths, so don't try to guess\n710: \t\t\t// what's needed here and return the proposed part of the value.\n711: \t\t\t// This is only a helper to create a default plan value, any tests\n712: \t\t\t// relying on specific plan behavior will create their own\n713: \t\t\t// PlanResourceChange responses.\n714: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n715: \t\t}\n716: \n717: \t\tswitch {\n718: \t\tcase attrSchema.Computed && !attrSchema.Optional && v.IsNull():\n719: \t\t\t// this is the easy path, this value is not yet set, and _must_ be computed\n720:             "content": "291: In some cases, flattening and expanding need conditional handling.\n292: One important case is new AWS API implementations where the input or output structs make use of [union types](https://smithy.io/2.0/spec/aggregate-types.html#union).\n293: The AWS implementation uses an interface as the common type, along with various concrete implementations.\n294: Because the Terraform schema does not support union types (see [this issue](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/32587) for discussion), the provider defines nested schemas for each type with a restriction to allow only one.\n295: \n296: To override flattening behavior, implement the interface `flex.Flattener` on the model.\n297: The function should have a pointer receiver, as it will modify the struct in-place.\n298: ",
